< Review>
I just moved from our 6300 square foot home (16 rooms + 2 stuffed garages!) in the San Diego area to a much smaller home in Encinitas and the Atlas team did an outstanding job moving us!

All 6 guys - Tyler, David, Alfonso, Lewis, Tre and Ernie - were awesome and worked really well together as a team. They were super friendly and helpful the entire time. During the move, I was really impressed with how they communicated with each other and also to us - to make sure everything was moved exactly from and to where we wanted. It was so much stuff since we had lived there for 20 years and there were many details to remember, but they executed perfectly. They kept all the like things together and that made for really efficient unloading and unpacking later on - but I will get to that in a minute.

The process for everything was very professionally done - Traci, you nailed it! First, a detailed quote was provided (by John- thank you!) a few weeks beforehand to set expectations and to buy packing materials, then I picked up the materials from their warehouse in Poway where they loaded me up with almost 200 boxes of varying sizes, including mattress bags and wardrobe boxes. Reminder calls were made by Traci to confirm we were on time, and we even received introduction calls the day of the move to let us know when they were on the way. When they arrived, they all got a house tour and I filled in the crew on details about our particular move. They prepped by throwing down red padded carpet all throughout the house, then they "Saran-wrapped" furniture and other delicate items. After that, they moved everything with padded dollies or by hand. And these guys are super strong because we have a lot of heavy pieces! The boxes were staged in our driveway as the vans on the street were carefully packed.

Not one thing was broken or damaged in the move and that is incredible given the sheer volume of what was moved. I did all/most of the packing myself the week before using their materials to speed up the process - and that really paid off because we ended up only taking 1 day instead of 2, saving us a lot of time and money. I really love the flexibility they gave the lead driver, Tyler, to make that decision on move day - and he was spot on! Once the truck was unloaded, we reviewed the placement of everything and in some cases we moved a few items around to see how we liked the fit -that alone probably saved us from trying to move some heavy things ourselves later.

Also, a 3rd party company subcontracted by Atlas took apart our home gym and did an excellent job: Hector from Moving Specialty Services, thank you!

It's been a few days since our move and we are happily settling in for what we hope is a very long time...but if I do ever have to move again, I'm calling Traci at Atlas. Best movers ever!<//Review>

Great little used appliance shop, my washer broke down on me and I happened upon this little store in my desperate search to find something quickly and inexpensively. The young woman in the store was very helpful and knowledgeable about the different brands. I ended up purchasing a used washing machine and they were able to deliver and install it the same day. Gas is gas except when you're out.  Furnace Creek and Stovepipe Wells are the only stations in the Park.  They are both a bit more expensive than an urban setting, but what did you expect! < review>
H Cabinet is a warehouse, no frills. Everything is on display. They have cabinets, cabinet knobs, flooring, kitchen countertops of various materials, and stainless steel sinks. You browse and select then a rep will help you. If you bring your measurements they will put your cabinet selections in a CAD presentation. They will load your truck and you're done. They also offer cabinet assembly.
The parking lot is small, but it turns over quickly.< /review>

<Review>Been going here for 3 years 4-5x a week, can't say I can relate to those people having parking issues since I always walk here. The staff members are usually friendly with a hello and good bye. I've been to ones back home in LA where they don't say a thing. So any acknowledgment is fine.

Gym:
It's not updated with the newest equipment like other 24 hr Fitness gyms. Probably due to the size constraints of the building and the lower foot traffic than those in the city. It has everything you need to make gains but could definitely use a renovation. The free weights are in the "basement" section where the musk gathers. Even though it may not have the newest bells and whistles it never gets overly crowded and I can get my workout in fairly quickly. If you think otherwise, you haven't gone to gyms in LA...

Bathroom:
Its pretty terrible. The mens stalls are small as hell, like literally shoulder to shoulder inside a piss infested death box. The lockers are standard and no signs of attempts of breaking in. I trust this gym. They do have 2 private stalls outside of the locker rooms for both men and women to use. It comes with a shower, toilet, and sink for those uncomfortable showering around others. That is something I haven't really seen at other 24s.

Overall: It's a gym and if you need all the fancy equipment go pay an arm and a leg with Equinox or Crunch. For 15 a month it works perfectly for me. If they ever get better equipment for every section I would update this to a 4-5 star.</Review><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Resp>

<text>I've been going here since February 2016 and have been going approximately 5 times per week (sometimes 4, sometimes 6). It's definitely a negative change from the previous 24 hour facilities I used to go to in Fremont and Hayward. In fact, I've never been to a gym in such poor condition.

Gym Equipment: It has almost everything you need for a full body weighted workout. It gets cramped at the usual times of the day. Kettle bells are hidden from members and only accessible with a trainer (which I had for a short period of time). There is a stretch room with mirrors, but lacks more space for more full body workouts. At peak times, between 530p-730p you often have to weight a while to get a bench, and definitely always a long weight for a squat rack. There's a lack of plates and I'm always wandering for days to find what I need at any station. There's a lack of space, but there are also a lack of benches for the dumbbell station.

Locker room: Absolutely the worst and smelliest locker room I've ever been in. It is very narrow so it is hard to move in and out or even take out your stuff from a locker to change without being interrupted several times by people trying to pass by. The showers is just a room with shower heads, no stalls, and the there are only two urinals which are always filled with piss and don't flush and two stalls which usually are working but often full.

Cardio: There is one row of treadmills and it's usually generally easy to get one; I've only had to wait a few times and they are in decent shape. The are four stair climbers which are usually full, but the rest of the cardio equipment: ellipticals always have an opening.

Parking: On top of my monthly payment (I pay $49.99 to have access to all 24 hour gyms across the country including super sport), I have to pay about $5/day whenever I come to this gym for parking. At peak times there's just no other choice. It adds up quick and is a pain.

Staff: I read reviews calling the staff unfriendly. I don't think this is true. They all have been friendly and helpful to me. I had a trainer for a short period of time and that was very easy to set up. They all say hello and goodbye. I don't know what people are expecting from the staff.

Overall: You're probably wondering, if it's so bad, why am I still a member? I'll start by saying, I've signed up for the new Club Sport in Berkeley that has not yet opened; I hear it will open in September, but not sure. There are two main reasons: 1) It is the closest and most affordable to where I live, and while I've thought about joining UC Berkeley's RSF (just a little more expensive) I've stayed. 2) I travel a lot, I have to visit Fremont a lot and work in Vallejo; I also find myself in cities across the United States often, and it is very nice to have the option of finding a gym anywhere I go. When I'm staying SF I go to the 24s there, I was just in Orlando and went to a great one there; it's a benefit that would be hard to find with a non-chain gym.

I started this review with 3 stars and as I wrote more, I kept bringing it down because I'm rating the actual gym, not the 24 hours fitness chain which I actually like.<//text><Time>1471235158715< /Time>< Resp>

<userid>118417939282901838818< /userid><user_name>Wan ker</user_name><Time>1539044997133</Time><Rate>5</Rate>< text>
GREAT FOOD & SERVICE! My wife and I were heading back home to Solana beach after visiting her Mom nearby. We Googled food and thankfully a Habit Burger Grill came up about a mile away.The place was very busy when we walked in the front door around 1.30pm but very quickly it was our turn. I even had a quick chat with one of the managers named Brittany while waiting in line. Another manager named Dave served us very efficiently at the cashier desk when we ordered a Teriyaki Charburger and a Tri-Tip Steak Sandwich on sourdough with Teriyaki Sauce.We found a booth table at the rear of the eatery and very soon our food pager went off.Our lunch tasted very fresh, full of quality ingredients, very well presented & most of all...delicious! It was very relaxing to sit in a pristine store and enjoy a very nice lunch before recommencing our long drive home.</text>
